-110-                       ANNEX5
ANNEX 5: ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT
SUMMARY
A. INTRODUCTION
Project Concept
1.    The EIA report for the project was based on the utilization and updating of earlier
studies of the project, which will meet the requirements of MWR, NEPA, Shanxi
Environmental Protection Bureau (EPB), and the World Bank.
2.    The EIA methodology utilized was that described in NEPA's EIA Guidelines
Modules now routinely used by NEPA and many provincial EPBs. This methodology
classifies environmental resources into four categories: (a) natural physical resources,
(b) natural biological resources, (c) human development resources, and (d) quality-of-life
resources. This identifies and evaluates the significant environmental issues (SEIs), i.e.,
potentials for adverse effects posed by the project components, and arranges for
modifications in the project planning so the net overall environmental impact will be
acceptable. In addition, an overall Environmental Management Plan (EMP) is prepared,
to be implemented when the project proceeds, and an Environmental Management Office
(EMO) is established, within the overall Project Management Structure, with
responsibility for implementing the EMP.
B. PROJECT DESCRIPTION
3.    Detailed project description is in Chapter 3 and Annex 1 of the SAR. The
description of the environmental components is summarized below.
Environmental Protection Components
4.    Generally, each of the various components of the project has been designed to
incorporate environmental protection measures as specified in the project EIA.  In
addition to the project's physical components, the overall present project includes (a) an
environmental training program, (b) an environmental monitoring program, for both
construction and operation stages, (c) a public participation program, and (d) an
Environmental Management Plan with an Environmental Management Office for
implementing the Environmental Management Plan.
Project Alternatives
5.    The decision to import water to Taiyuan from Wanjiazhai reservoir is based on
extensive studies that show that this is the only feasible solution. No more water, either



-111-                       ANNEX5
surface or groundwater, is available locally, hence import of water is essential, and import
from Wanjiazhai represents by far the lowest cost system.
6.    With current water shortages in the Project Areas amounting to 40 percent of
estimated demand, and growing rapidly, and both groundwater and surface water supplies
declining, failure to complete the project would engender economic, social, and
envirornmental calamity. Projections using the Provincial Planning Model (PPM) show
that if the project area urban residents are to be given supplies equaling the norms for
China, and if farmers water allocations are to be preserved at current levels, industrial and
mining activities would decline rapidly and virtually cease after the year 2010. It is not
surprising that Chinese planners have mentioned the possibility that the Taiyuan/Datong
industries would need to be relocated (at incalculable cost) if project water is not
forthcoming.
C. ENVIRONMENTAL SETTING
Environmental Study Area (ESA)
7.    The EIA Main Report (not included here) includes drawings that show the EIAs
for each of the Phase I EIA component studies, namely Wanjiazhai Reservoir, GMT,
SMT, Fen- l Reservoir, Connection Works, and the Taiyuan Service Area.
Land Use
8.    The overall project ESA is primarily hilly and mountainous and the land use in
the area can be broadly categorized into farmland, garden plot, forest, grassland, urban
and industrial area, infrastructure, water area, and wasteland area. Land use in the ESA
has long been impacted by human activities, primarily agriculture, and the impact has
been particularly severe on the area's forest and wildlife resources. The land use impact
of the project per se will be essentially limited to the vicinity of the projects ground-
surface components.
Natural Physical Resources
9.    The project region enjoys temperate/seasonal/continental zone type of climate, is
drought prone, and the annual precipitation ranges between 430 and 480 mm.
10.   The project passes through several major tectonic features, including two seismic
zones. The Pianguan river, a tributary of the Yellow River, constitutes the major surface
hydrology for the GMT, and the Pianguan, Jian-er, and Fen rivers for the SMT.
Groundwater along the project is of good quality and suitable for community use
purposes.



-112 -                       ANNEX5
Natural Biological Resources
11.   The natural biological resources in Phase I/ESA  may be categorized into
(a) forests and other vegetation, (b) terrestrial wildlife, and (c) aquatic ecology (see Table
8).
12.   With respect to animal wildlife in the ESA, because of low vegetation coverage
the animal habitats are limited. A total of 133 animal species are found, including 31
species of resource animals and some 16 species of State-protected animals including 4 in
the Class I rare category. However, all of the project component facilities (excluding
tunnels) are located in already humanized developed areas. All of the protected species
live in areas remote from the project components locations/activities; hence, they should
not be affected by the project.
13.   With respect to aquatic species, the ESA waterways contain relatively few aquatic
plants and aquatic animals. There are some 17 species of fish but these have no
commercial value and all are hardly of value even for subsistence. There are no known
rare aquatic species that would be affected. The Fen River is heavily affected by
Taiyuan, by extractions and pollution discharges, and has no significant remaining
aquatic species of value.
Development Resources
14.   The area along the GMT lines is primarily an agricultural region with limited
farming and livestock because of limited water and mountainous terrain. Crops like
millet, beans, corn, oats, potato, sesame, broomcorn millet, and fruits like apple, pears
and grapes are grown. Livestock development is mainly sheep raising. Agricultural
production is also low in the SMT area because of poor landform and unfavorable
climatic conditions, although it still is the main source of income for local people.
15.   With respect to urbanization/industrialization, most of the project area is hilly and
mountainous resulting in limited urban industrial development in the region.
Quality of Life Resources
16.   Shanxi Province, including the project ESA, represents one of the poorest regions
in China, despite the presence of considerable mineral resources including the coal
mining and power industries. The people in the ESA, in their reliance on economic
income sources, are in roughly two categories: (a) those in urban centers who are
working mainly in industry, and (b) rural villagers who depend mainly on agriculture.
The latter are much poorer than the former. By far the most important parameter, which
is crippling the continuing development of the province, is lack of water supply for all
sectors of development. This includes both the urban/industrial sector, which represents
the backbone of the overall economic/socioeconomic resources of the province, and the
rural farning sector where the people are very poor despite availability of adequate farm
land areas.



-113 -                      ANNEX5
17.   There are no precious archeological relics or monuments of historical or special
culture located in any of the project component areas.
D. ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT AND EPMs
Delineation of Significant Environmental Issues (SEIs)
18.   The essential findings of the EIA process, namely (a) delineation of the SEIs,
(b) evaluation of each of these to make a quantified assessment of the potentials for
adverse environmental effects if no Environmental Protection Measures (EPMs) are
utilized, and (c) delineation and quantification of the needed EPMs so that the project will
be economically sound. Needs for environmental monitoring during the construction and
operation stages are concerned with the water transfer system, which will deliver the
imported water to Taiyuan City (to the Huyan Water Treatment Plant), and focuses on
use of the imported water by the City.
19.   The SEIs identified and evaluated by the project EIA are listed as follows (see
Table 1):
(a)   Critical need for additional water for Taiyuan service area;
(b)   Availability of water for diversion to Taiyuan;
(c)   Delivery system:
(i)    Resettlement
(ii)    Assurance of continuing delivery of imported water
(iii)    Maintenance of water quality
(iv)    Construction operations constraints
(v)    Disposal of tunnel excavation materials
(vi)    Siltation problems;
(d)   Use of imported water at Taiyuan:
(i)    Appropriate use of both imported water and local water resource
including reuse
(ii)    Water management and pollution control/water quality in Fen
River
(iii)    Coordination of (i) and (ii) for optimal overall water use and
pollution control system;



-114 -                      ANNEX5
(e)   Overall
(i)    Environmental monitoring during construction and operation
stages
(ii)    Environmental Management Plan and Office
(iii)    Environmental/Training.
Evaluation of SEIs
Land Use
20.   The significant impacts of the project on land use for Phase I will be in
(a) acquisition of land for the transmission line facilities that are aboveground, including
construction camps, and (b) land needed for disposal of tunnel excavation materials. This
totals some 659 ha, of which 166 ha will be used only temporarily. About 579 ha of the
required land is farmland. However, the reduction of farmland, both permanent and
temporary, should not have any significant impacts on farming in the region traversed by
the Phase I project because this only represents less than 0.1 of 1 percent of the farmland in
the region.
Hydrology
21.   Environmental Concerns. The environmental concerns on project hydrology
relates to the effects caused by the water transmission system along its route, and on
beneficial uses of both surface water and groundwater resources, both during the
construction and operation stages.  The effects due to the construction stage are
temporary, whereas those during the operation stage are continuing.
22.   Surface Water. The planned project, when completed, will divert annually from
Wanjiazhai Reservoir 640 million m3 water to Taiyuan Service Area and 560 million m3
to the Pingshuo and Datong Service Areas when these are connected. However, for
Phase 1, limited to SMT, only 640 million m3 will be diverted. No reservoirs are included
in Phase I, but Phase I will utilize the existing Fen-1 reservoir for regulation purposes.
The diverted water will have significant positive impacts on the surface water hydrology
in the three service areas. Assuming the recommended EPMs are properly followed and
implemented during both construction and operation stages, the project is expected to
have no significant negative impacts on hydrology in the Project ESA. Use of Fen-I
reservoir for regulating purposes will not adversely affect the existing function of this
reservoir.
23.   Flooding and Siltation Hazards. Flooding hazards are very unlikely to be
caused by tunnel failures because the tunnels are deeply in the ground. But flood hazards
may be caused by pipe, aqueduct, or culvert failures due to earthquakes, poor operations,
and poor construction quality. When such failure occurs, the monitoring and control



-115 -                      ANNEX5
system to be established along the project will function to stop the diversion immediately,
so the water released out the pipe or aqueducts is limited to only the water volume in the
transmission line between two nearest valves (gates), which are designed to be promptly
closed.
24.   The only existing stream to which the diverted water will be discharged is the Fen
River on SMT. While the imported water volume will be about the same as the average
river flow, the imported volume will represent less than 1 percent of the Fen River flood
flow peaks. Hence, the effect of the imported water on Fen River hydrology is expected
to be negligible. With respect to the impact of the silt content of the imported water on
Fen River siltation, the volume of imported silt is only about 3 percent of that in the river
from local runoff; hence, the effect of the imported water will be to alleviate existing
siltation problems.
25.   Groundwater. All of the tunnels on the GMT and SMT are located above
groundwater, so no groundwater problems are expected, in either construction or
operations. Because there are no villages along the tunnel routes, and limited farmland,
the tunnel operations are not expected to exert any negative impact on groundwater use
by villagers along these routes.
26.   Water for construction will be obtained from wells built by the Construction
Contractors. The wells to be utilized must be stated and identified by each Construction
Contractors (CC) at the time of his proposal, and the CC must arrange to obtain the water
he needs without impairment of existing beneficial water users and/or with the
concurrence of the existing users.
27.   The construction well will lower the groundwater table to some extent during the
construction period. However, the impacts should not be significant because the wells
are located far from existing wells, will extract from areas not conflicting with existing
wells, and the amounts withdrawn for each well is small (less than 1,000 m3/day).
28.   Monitoring Program for Hydrology. The Project's EMO will routinely check
the CC's operations as related to effects on hydrology, so that all potentials for adverse
effects will be suitably controlled for the purposes of expediting construction and for
avoiding and/or offsetting any conflicts with existing beneficial water uses. Following
completion of construction, the EMO will carry out periodic monitoring of effects of
project operations on hydrology in ESA, including water quality. Details of these
monitoring programs for hydrology for both construction and operations stages are given
in the EIA Main Report.
Special Design Issues
29.   Tunnel Hazards. The concerns here are that (a) the tunnel design take into
account the earthquake hazard in the region, (b) provision be made in the tunnel design to
enable prompt repair of tunnel failures, (c) the overall project plan will include sufficient
storage in the system's reservoirs to that the system can continue to function in the event



-116 -                      ANNEX5
of failure of delivery of water because of tunnel collapse or any other reason, and (d) the
tunnel construction methods will include adequate attention to worker health and safety.
In general the overall plan for the project will furnish two months' storage for the target
service area in order to (i) enable shutdown of delivery from Wanjiazhai for two months,
and (ii) furnish enough storage to overcome the hazard of tunnel collapse. Use of the
existing Fen-I reservoir for regulation will furnish the needed two months of storage.
With respect to Item (d) above, in order to ensure adequate protection for tunnel workers,
YRDP has changed the method for tunnel construction to use shield-protected core-
boring machines, which do ensure adequate protection.
30.   Equipment Erosion Hazards. Because of the high turbidity of the Yellow
River, the concern here is whether the pumps and other equipment will be eroded by silt
and thus not be able to function throughout their design life period. Project study reports
on this subject note that the turbidities will not exceed levels of 3,000 to 4,000 ppm and
that this does not represent a serious constraint to pump equipment suppliers.
31.   Reservoir Intake Hazards/Frazile Ice. This hazard is whether there will be
reservoir intake problems due to entry of ice and/or "frazile" (a kind of ice mush); hence,
the design will incorporate special precautions to guard against this hazard. In response
to this problem, YRDP design staff have developed a special type of intake design which
involves use of a weir with a grill which warms the frazile to turn it into harmless mush
which is readily managed.
32.   Disposal of Tunnel Excavation Materials. A special environmental problem for
project Phase I construction is disposal of tunnel excavation materials so as not to cause
environmental damage including damage to lands better used for farming, creation of
flooding hazards, hazards of runoff of these materials to cause pollution/damage, and
despoiling of environmental scenery. For these reasons, the project Phase I planning
includes provision of detailed schemes so that disposal will be accomplished in a manner
which is environmentally sound, as presented in the EIA Main Report Section 4.11.4,
including Figure 4.11.4-1.
33.   Silt Deposition Problems. The concern here is whether the silt in the imported
water might interfere with the project operations. The analysis of this problem shows that
the silt content of the imported water is only a small fraction, 3 percent, of the silt carried
by runoff from the Fen River watershed above Fen-1 reservoir; hence the importation
should actually alleviate existing siltation problems.
Environmental Review of Resettlement (ERR)
34.   Purpose and Scope of Task. The EIA Main Report reviews and assess the
environmental soundness of the resettlement (RS) plan presented in the project RS
Report, to ensure that the recommended RS plan will include all needed attention to
applicable environmental parameters, including effects on the RS families, on host
villages/families, and affected community/regional infrastructure.



-117 -                     ANNEX5
35.   The plan also gives due attention to the timeliness of the various RS process
components, so that preparation of the new situation facilities (houses, land, etc.) will be
ready for use at the scheduled time for moving residences and/or land uses. Because the
project does not include any new reservoirs, the RS problem is relatively small for the
project components included in Phase I. However, for EIA purposes, the overall ERR
also includes Wanjiazhai reservoir, which has a large RS problem, and the Huyan Water
Treatment Plant (and related pumping plant), which involves significant urban RS
problems.
36.   Approach for Preparing ERR. For ERR purposes, on the basis of the types of
RS problems involved, the overall ERR study has been divided into four categories as
follows:
(a)   GMT: Disturbance in rural areas to both housing and farm production
lands.
(b)   SMT and CWs:  Disturbances in rural communities only on farm
production lands, with no housing losses.
(c)   Huyan: Only urban land use changes, with no housing losses.
(d)   Wanjiazhai: Major disturbances in rural communities including both
housing and farm production lands.
37.   The project ERR has been patterned after the ERR done a few years ago for the
Xiaolangdi project. This includes several major categories, with various subcategories,
for the issues of (a) accommodating RS families, (b) accommodating host communities,
(c) regional infrastructure needs, (d) public participation, (e) monitoring plan adequacy,
and (f) overall assessment.
38.   Summary, Conclusions, and Monitoring. Review of this information indicates
that the RS Planning programs are reasonable adequate for all four RS sectors. However,
the YRDP EMO will monitor the RS progress periodically for all Phase I components
(GMT, SMT, CWs) and also with check progress for Wanjiazhai, working with the
Wanjiazhai EMO, and for Huyan, working with TEPB. This includes checking on
progress on the Phase I RS training program. In addition, the Expert Panel for
Environment and Resettlement to be established by YRDPC is also expected to make
periodic reviews and recommendations for all RS sector projects.
Public Health
39.   The significant hazards for the EIA include both enteric diseases due to
inadequate sanitation and insect vector diseases, namely encephalitis and hemorrhagic
fever. Both the construction and operation stages of the project are involved.



-118 -                       ANNEX5
40.   The recommended action program for enteric diseases and insect vector diseases
control includes the following:
(a)    Enteric Diseases:  The project's construction program  will include
provisions for protection against outbreaks of enteric diseases such as
typhoid and dysentery, by (i) provision of adequate and safe water supply
and sanitation facilities for construction workers and (ii) medical
examination (initial and periodic) for construction workers. Also the
housing buildings for construction workers should be periodically sprayed
with insecticides for mosquito control.
(b)   Insect Vector Diseases:  Phase I Project will not finance any dams/
reservoirs nor any irrigation facilities, hence Phase I will not affect these
diseases. However, it is recommended that the Phase I Project monitoring
program will include close check on incidence of these three diseases in
the overall project region and if any significant increases occur, then
special control measures should be implemented. During Phase I, it will
be necessary to monitor rat densities in the construction zones, which may
tend to increase due to the food available there, and if significant increases
occur, rat killing measures should be carried out to prevent increases in
hemorrhagic fever due to the project.
Ecology
41.   The project's Phase I will convey water to the Taiyuan Service Area by passing
through the following areas in sequence, (a) mountainous zone, where the facilities are
underground, (b) the Fen river, over a reach of some 81.2 km, (c) the Connection Works
region, for delivery of water from Fen- 1 reservoir to the Taiyuan Service Area.
42.   Effects on ecology in the mountainous zone will be negligible because the system
facilities are essentially underground. There are some 22 species of State protected
species in the mountain areas, but these are remote from urbanizing/industrializing areas
and should not be affected by the project.
43.   There will be an impact on the Fen River reach utilized for conveyance, above
Fen-l reservoir, both for flora and fauna. At present, this river reach includes no valuable
fishery, not even for subsistence, and no valuable rare species. Because the overall
project will include rigid control of pollution discharges to the river, including industrial
discharges, and because the project will add clean fresh water which will increase the
river flow volume, the river water quality should be significantly improved and this
should significantly improve habitats for both flora and fauna. The introduction of
different species from Wanjiazhai reservoir will modify the eco-balance in the river and
in Fen-1 reservoir but this should hardly affect the overall aquatic ecology in the region.
44.   The natural ecology in both the Connection Works area and Taiyuan Service Area
have been essentially displaced by existing development.



-119 -                       ANNEX5
Reservoir EIAs
45.   Wanjiazhai Reservoir. The Wanjiazhai EIA shows that the project should not
cause any significant problems of enviromnental degradation, provided it is designed and
operated as planned, including incorporation of the EPMs specified in the EIA and
including environmental monitoring in both construction and operation stages, and
including implementation of provisions for resettlement as specified in the Phase I
Project RS report (see Table 10). A potential adverse effect on the project is the silt
content of the diverted water (about I percent) in possibly causing siltation/flooding
problems in the Fen river system, but the EIA analysis shows that silt content of the
imported water is much less than in the Fen River (3.3 percent), hence the effects of
importation will be beneficial. The project will result in large-scale positive benefits
including flood control and power production and availability of water for export to the
project target areas. Export of Wanjiazhai water for the project will decrease the total
water availability in the Lower Yellow River Basin, but the approved overall
governmental plan for allocation of the Yellow River water resource includes provisions
for project diversion needs.
46.   Fen-1 Reservoir.  Use of Fen-1 reservoir for project regulation, following
construction, will bring about minor changes in reservoir hydrology, but without adverse
effects, and the impact on the existing flood protection function of the reservoir will be
small compared to that from local runoff, hence no adverse effects are expected. The
imported water inflow will result in some shift in the reservoir aquatic ecology balance,
but this should not result in any adverse effects on the reservoir fishery nor on the
regional aquatic ecology.
47.   Erosion and Sedimentation. Assuming that the contracts for the CCs include
provisions as noted in the section on "Construction Constraints" and assuming proper use
of environmental construction inspectors, construction of the project will not cause any
significant erosion problems. Also, because the diverted silt represents only a small
amount of the total silt reaching the Fen River course and Fen-l Reservoir, around 3
percent, no significant impacts are expected on sedimentation in the areas along SMT.
Quality of Life
48.   People Living along Water Transmission System. The only significant effect
of the project's transmission system will be impacts on people whose houses or lands will
be taken over and utilized for these facilities. There are only a small number of such
families, and all of their losses will be compensated for, at rates such that the net effect is
expected to be beneficial for all affected families.
49.   Taiyuan Service Area (TSA).  The project will certainly result in great
improvements in quality of life in TSA, all made possible by the availability of the
imported water to alleviate the existing severe water shortage. These benefits include
(a) considerably increased family income resulting from improved industrial productivity,
(b) marked increase in per capita water use, so that residents will have decent amounts of



-120 -                      ANNEX5
water for washing and bathing and for toilets, (c) significant decrease in disease rates for
enteric diseases, stemming from steady availability of pipe water to homes/buildings, and
(d) great improvements in urban greening areas and in urban recreational areas.
Construction Constraints
50.   Historically  CCs have often caused unnecessary  environmental damage,
sometimes serious, simply because it is the nature of the CC, and of the Engineering
Supervision of Construction, to focus on expediting building of the project physical
components, with relatively low-priority attention to EPMs. However, experience has
shown that it is quite feasible/affordable for the CC to observe and comply with the
EPMs specified in EIA. These will be included in the terms of reference (TOR) for the
CC's construction contract and ECIs will be made available by EMO to observe the CC's
operations and to require compliance. Main Report Figures 4.11.2-1 and 4.11.4-1
summarize the details.
Interbasin Water Transfer Feasibility
51.   The project has been an approved component of the Government's overall Yellow
River Basin Plan for the past two decades. This will divert about 2 percent of the mean
annual river flow and about 5 percent of dry-year flows, but the Wanjiazhai storage is
from periods of higher river flow, and this should not pose hardships on downstream
water users. This issue was further investigated using the Bank's Basin Level Planning
Model. These studies confirmed that the project will not create problems for the
downstream users assuming that all "Shareholders" of the river do not extract more than
their allocated share.
Connection Works
52.   The EIA for the CWs (Connection Works), described in EIA Main Report Section
4.13, notes that (a) because the CWs are located in already developed areas, there will be
no adverse effects on forests/wildlife, (b) no adverse effects on aquatic ecology (in Fen
River and Fen-1 Reservoir) are expected, (c) no adverse effects on Fen-1 Reservoir
existing operating functions are expected, (d) no effect on archeological/historic or
cultural values are expected, (e) there will be some use of land now used for other
purposes, but only some 16 ha permanently and 235 ha on a temporary basis, (f) there
will be no significant changes in the quality of the imported water due to river passage
and reservoir storage, and (g) the only significant hazard for environment will be that for
the construction stage.
Global Environmental Issues
53.   The primary environmental concerns, from  the global point of view, are:
(a) earth-warming, (b) ozone layer increase, and (c) biological diversity degradation.



-121-                      ANNEX5
54.   Because the project components that are aboveground are in areas that are already
"humanized," with little significant remaining natural ecological resources, the project is
not expected to have any significant effects on the biodiversity situation in the ESA
region. However, the monitoring program to be managed by EMO will include an annual
survey of the status of ecology in ESA including forests, swamps, and wildlife.
55.   The project does not involve use or production of substances to be discharged to
atmosphere which will contribute to ozone layer depletion.
56.   The project will require expenditure of a considerable amount of electrical energy
for enabling pumping of the imported water into the service areas, but this total amount is
insignificant in terms of China's production of earth warming gases from burning of coal.
Hence, the project should have no significant impact on China's total contribution to
earth warming.
Water Supply, Uses and Pollution Control
57.   Water Supply and Use. Annex 7 of the SAR shows the new water supply, water
demand and balance for the Taiyuan Service Area, which will result from water imported
by the project.
58.   Water Pollution Control. The project will generate wastewater that will have to
be managed, along with existing wastewaters, so that significant environmental pollution
impacts are properly controlled and managed. The increased wastewater volumes that
will result in Taiyuan from new water have been forecasted for the years 2002, 2010, and
2020. Assuming that primary treatment is required for agricultural reuse, and that
secondary treatment is required for discharge and for agricultural and industrial reuse,
Taiyuan City has developed a plan to increase wastewater treatment capabilities to almost
100 percent for the target years. The plan is summarized in the following:
Year                             1995       2002       2010        2020
Wastewater Flow, 104 m3/day        65         114        156        207
Treatment, % of Total
Primary                            0          7         32         51
Secondary                         19         51         42         42
Tertiary                           0          0          0          7
Stabilization Pond                 0         38         26          0
Treated Wastewater %                19        96         100        100
59.   The plan calls for use of stabilization ponds in the tributaries of Fen River and
along the banks of Fen River to provide additional treatment when wastewater collection



-122 -                      ANNEX5
and treatment plants are being built. The target is to phase out stabilization ponds and
have sufficient collection systems and treatment plants in use by 2020.
60.   Cost estimates for treating wastewater generated until the year 2020 have been
developed. The estimated treatment costs for the period until 2020 are about Y 2.8
billion.
Water Quality
61.   The impact of the planned project water conveyance system on the quality of the
imported water should not be significant for all salient water quality parameters because
the system will comprise mostly tunnels and culverts that will be enclosed. However, the
receiving Fen River is an open stream and will be vulnerable to contamination. This will
require the waste management program mentioned in the section on "Water Pollution
Control."
62.   The quality of the raw water delivered to Taiyuan and other service areas will
correspond to Class III in the National Government's classification system. Based on the
available date on Yellow River water quality at Wanjiazhai and elsewhere in the Yellow
River system, it appears that the imported water delivered to the service areas will be
suitable for a raw water supply for all intended uses, with treatment needed to meet
drinking water standards. Conventional rapid sand filtration with effluent chlorination
should meet this need.
63.   The project is not expected to adversely affect groundwater quality in the ESA
except during the construction stages when use of groundwater by the CC must be strictly
controlled.
64.   Assuming implementation of the treatment program described in the section on
"Water Pollution Control," it is expected that the water quality in Fen River will not be
adversely impacted by wastewater discharges. The predicted pollution concentration in
the Fen River would be much lower than the current condition (see Table 11).
Integrated Management of Water Supply/Use/Pollution Control
65.   To ensure that industries and municipalities will treat their wastewater prior to
discharge, an area-wide regulatory/implementation agency will be established as shown
in Figure 3. This is to perform the functions currently being accomplished by several
governmental agencies with the following responsibilities:
(a)   Regulating water use to ensure optimal overall use of the limited water
supply, with priority to substitute use of treated effluent by industries in
place of using freshwater, and use of treated effluents for other reuse
purposes including agricultural irrigation and groundwater recharging, so
that freshwater use is limited to priority purposes. This will be achieved
by use of an appropriate pricing structure and by monitoring/enforcement.



-123 -                     ANNEX5
(b)   Establishing appropriate standards for wastewater treatment and for reuse
of treated wastewater as water supply.
(c)   Strengthening the existing permit system to be similar to that used in the
United States, so all industries which produce significant wastes (liquid
and solid) will build/operate their own treatment systems as needed to
protect environment. The permit system involves establishing appropriate
discharge standards, monitoring the quality of discharge effluents, and
enforcing the regulations through a penalty system for violators. River
water toxicity will be controlled, primarily by the use of the permit
system, so that existing discharges from industries will cease.
(d)   Establishing/maintaining  an environmental monitoring program  for
exercising surveillance on all waste treatment facilities, including sewage
treatment plants and solid waste disposal sites, and for ambient water
quality monitoring, as needed for achieving a comprehensive area-wide
monitoring program.
(e)   Establishing a water pricing mechanism to promote optimal water reuse.
(f)   Provision of an education and training of industrial and municipal staff
and the public about the significance of uncontrolled discharges and the
importance of waste management, to promote awareness and acceptance
of the program.
66.   The ultimate goal of the integrated management mechanics is to achieve the
optimal water use, reuse, and pollution control system shown in Figure 2. This would be
similar to the program of this type now in action in Southern California.
67.   The overall project loan includes an allocation of $8.0 million for establishing a
Clean Technologies Fund for industries.  This program  is consistent with and
supplementary and complementary to the recommendations made in the presents EIA.
Pollution Control Achievement at Taiyuan City
68.   Despite the many difficulties involved, the Taiyuan city agencies, working in
close cooperation with the Provincial agencies, have over the past decade made
impressive progress in planning and implementing a comprehensive water pollution
program in the Taiyuan service area. This includes:
(a)   Preparation of a comprehensive municipal sewerage management plan,
and implementation of the plan including treatment of some 19 percent of
the total city sewage, with planning to achieve comprehensive control by
year 2020.



-124 -                     ANNEX5
(b)   Establish of an initial permit system for control of industrial waste
discharg_s, resulting in much more plant recycling and use of in-plant
treatment to meet discharge requirements including reduction in discharge
of heavy metals.
(c)   Establishment of the initial comprehensive water quality monitoring
program, covering both pollution sources and ambient water quality of
receiving waters, to gain factual data on the extent and nature of waste
management problems.
(d)   Initiation of other measures including public education on water
conservation, reducing leakage in water supply distribution, and
promoting industrial water reuses and other reuse of treated effluents.
69.   These activities represent a good beginning step towards achieving optimal water
use/reuse/pollution control, and are firm evidence of the keen interest of the local officials
in striving to solve their water use/pollution problems and of their willingness to give real
support to achieving the goals of the proposed project.
E. PUBLIC PARTICIPATION
Public Participation (PP)
70.   YRDP has been active in PP work on the project even since initial establishment
of YRDP in the 1950s. These activities have increased over the years, as YRDP's role
has expanded, with detailed attention beginning in 1992.  Considerable public
participation has been taking place during 1993-97, through involvement of counties in
the project preparation activities.
Compliance with Environmental Laws
71.   Both NEPA and the World Bank require that the EIA include information
showing how the project complies with China's environmental laws and regulations. The
full-scale EIA study has included such attention to all known environmental laws and
regulations applicable to the project.
Environmental Economics
72.   The project may truly be said to be a project planned with the primary objectives
of improving the socioeconomics of the primary economic-earning areas of Shanxi
province. These are already critically short of water for virtually all human development
needs including (a) domestic and commercial, (b) industrial, and (c) agricultural needs.
The imported water will be used first for municipal purposes, with second priority to
industry to maintain employment stability, and then to agriculture. It is also planned to
reduce existing use of freshwater resources for agriculture by substituting use of treated
sewage effluents. In addition, the imported water will reduce pressures for more and



-125 -                     ANNEX5
more ground-level subsidence, already very serious and causing serious economic/
socioeconomic losses to all affected community sectors. Thus, the project may be said to
be a truly economic-cum-environmental-cum social development project.
73.   The argument may be made that the project favors the socioeconomics of the
urbanized target areas, which are less poor than the rural areas. This is true, but it is these
target areas that are of prime importance to the overall economy and socioeconomics of
the entire province. Also, where reservoirs are to be built as part of the project, it is
planned that the resettled rural farmers will be benefited, that is, their housing and income
levels will be improved as a result of the resettlement.
Risk Assessment
74.   Table 12 summarizes the Risk Assessment evaluation. The project is expected to
be a well engineered project and moreover should be financially sound because of the
precious value of the imported water for sustaining the economy of Shanxi Province. The
real risk, actually, is the risk that the project might not get built.
F. ENVIRONMENTAL MONITORING
Description of Monitoring Program
75.   An essential component of the overall project is its Environmental Monitoring
program, which is to cover both the construction and operations stages of the project, thus
covering a period of some 25 years. The monitoring work should begin as soon as the
Environmental Management Office becomes operative in June 1997. The summarized
monitoring program to be administered by EMO is shown in Tables 2, 3, 4 and 5,
including delineation of tasks and costs.
76.   The costs for professional EMO staffing are estimated at Y 13.04 million or
$1.5875 million for the total of 25.5 years (preconstruction 0.5 years, construction 5
years, operations 20 years), average $62,000 per year (see Table 6).
Management of Monitoring Program
77.   The monitoring program is to be managed and supervised by the EMO, with
much of the detailed field work done by the ECIs and some by the EMO office staff.
However, other agencies, including the provincial EPP. Hydrographic Station, AES, and
Shanxi University are to participate in the field work in accordance with agreements with
YRDPC. Costs for monitoring work by these other agencies, which is outside their
normal scope of monitoring, are to be reimbursed by YRDPC.
Importance of Monitoring Program
78.   Note that the overall monitoring program includes essentially two components:
(a) monitoring to ensure continuing delivery of water to the service area, and



-126 -                       ANNEX5
(b) monitoring to ensure optimal use of the imported (and expensive) water in the service
area, including monitoring of water use and reuse, waste management/water pollution
control, and Fen River water quality.
79.   The monitoring costs are significant but actually very small as related to total
project costs, and the benefit/cost ratio will be large. The monitoring data will be
essential for purposes of optimal water use planning and for this reason will result in
large savings through minimization of water wastage. The monitoring is absolutely
essential to the success of the project.
G. ENVIRONMENTAL TRAINING
Need for Training
80.   Implementation of the project will be a pioneering project for Shanxi Province in
transbasin diversion of water on a massive scale, for meeting the critical needs for more
water to support continuing growth and development of parched areas of northern China.
Because of the excessively high cost of such imported water, it is essential that
conventional practices on water use, waste treatment, water pollution control, and water
reuse be reoriented to achieve an integrated comprehensive program that makes
maximum/optimal use of the precious water for all essential water uses in the service
areas (Taiyuan Service Area for Phase I) including domestic, commercial, industrial, and
agricultural needs, including balanced use of all freshwater resources (local surface water,
local groundwater, and imported water), and including institutional, legal, economic, and
financing as well as engineering aspects.
Recommended Training
81.   In order to achieve this goal, a training program is needed to strengthen the
capabilities of the officials involved in the project including YRDPC, Shanxi Province,
and local agencies, in the various new approaches and methodologies which will be
utilized. The recommended training program, shown in Table 7, is a specialized training
program to be an integral part of the Phase I project. This program, to cost an estimated
$368,500, will include training by foreign experts of selected Chinese personnel who will
then conduct training courses at Taiyuan for stuff of participating agencies, plus a visit by
a selected team to foreign countries to study integrated water r ,e technologies developed
there over the past four decades.
Value of Training Program
82.   The proposed training program should prove to be one of the most cost-effective
components of the entire project. Its total cost is small, only a very small percentage of
total first-phase investment cost, but this small investment is essential if the precious
imported water is to be wisely used. It is expected that the training program will result in
more appropriate planning decisions on investments in facilities and thus result in savings
of tens of millions of dollars over the Phase I project design life period.



-127 -                     ANNEX5
H. ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PLAN (EMP)
Introduction
83.   The  Environmental Management Plan  (EMP) comprises  environmental
management activities and institutional arrangements, particularly the Environmental
Management Office (EMO), which is designed to ensure that all of the EPMs specified in
the EIA, including environmental monitoring, will be actually carried out.
Environmental Management System
84.   To ensure effective administration of environmental management, YRDP will
create the Environmental Management Lead Group and Environmental Management
Office (EMO), whose combined responsibility is the administration and implementation
of the EMP. The Lead Group will be comprised of senior officials of YRDP, the
provincial environmental agencies, and local agencies that will have responsibilities for
undertaking specific environmental management tasks. Figure 1 shows the institutional
roles of the EMO.
85.  In addition, YRDPC will establish an Expert Panel on Environment, comprising
distinguished foreign and Chinese experts, which will meet every six months to review
YRDP progress in implementing the Phase I's environmental (and resettlement) action
programs. The scope of work by EMO and Expert Panel is to include periodic review of
the progress of MWR Wanjiazhai Reservoir Management EMO in implementing the
EPMs specified in the EIA for Wanjiazhai.
Environmental Management Activities
86.   The overall environmental management activities are illustrated in Table 3.
EMO Costs and Justification
87.   The total costs as shown in Table 6 for the EMO EMP program are estimated to
be approximately $4.194 million, for a total period of 25.5 years including 0.5 years for
preconstruction activities, 5 years for construction, plus 20 years of operation. This
averages about $164,500 per year. This cost represents a very small percentage of the
total Phase I project cost, and is very much less than what is practiced in Western
countries for similar projects. Experience has shown that the benefit/cost ratio for this
investment is very high because it is essential to ensure that the project will be
economically-cum-environmentally sound, therefore sustainable.
I. SUMMARY AND CONCLUSIONS
EIA Team and Report
88.   The EIA has been carried out for YRDPC by CIRP/Shanxi University with the
assistance of WB/EIA team members, over the period July 1995 to July 1996. The EIA



-128-                      ANNEX5
Main Report and the Executive Summary Report have been prepared in both the Chinese
version (to meet NEPA requirements) and the English version (to meet World Bank
requirements). Both versions use the same Table of Contents and are essentially the same
in substance.
Management of Significant Environmental Issues
89.   Tables 8, 9 and 10 summarize the environmental impacts of the project. It (a) lists
all of the SEIs, (b) quantifies each in terms of potentials for adverse effects if not
controlled, of potentials for benefits with feasible controls, and of net effects with these
controls, (c) shows the EPMs measures which must be taken as part of the feasible
control system, and (d) shows the net environmental effects. Table 1 shows the control
measures and, assuming proper implementation of EPMs by the EMO, the project will
achieve great environmental benefits with virtually no significant environmental losses.
Xiaolangdi Experience
90.   Because conditions for the SEIs for the project are similar in many respects to the
SEIs for Xiaolangdi, the pioneering experience of the Xiaolangdi project in managing
these issues (including construction stage problems) furnishes very valuable guidelines
for project EIA purposes.

ANNEX 6: RESETTLEMENT AND REHABILITATION (R&R)
ACTION PLAN
A. INTRODUCTION
1.    This annex describes the land acquisition and resettlement impacts under the
project, the framework developed by Shanxi Provincial Government for implementation
of R&R activities and an evaluation of R&R programs completed. Resettlement planning
of Wanjiazhai Dam and Reservoir Project, financed by the Chinese Government alone
and indirectly linked with the project, is also described.
B. LAND ACQUISITION AND ADVERSE IMPACTS
2.    The following components of the project requires land acquisition:
(a)   General Main Tunnel (GMT). GMT component includes 11 tunnels, 3
pumping stations and 4 aqueducts. The total length is 44.35 km.
(b)   South Main Tunnel (SMT).  SMT consists of 103 km waterways
including 7 tunnels with a length of 98 km, 3 aqueducts and 2
aboveground pumping stations.
(c)   Connection Works. This component consists of 40.2 km of transmission
pipelines and 6 tunnels of 16.75 km.
(d)   Taiyuan Water Supply. This component includes a new water treatment
plant and two booster stations.
Census Survey
3.    Census surveys were undertaken on the physical losses for different components
of the project. The census surveys were conducted according to the "Detailed Rule And
Regulations on Physical Loss Survey of Reservoir Inundation for Water Conservancy
And Hydropower Projects" by the Ministry of Water Resources (MWR). The surveys
were conducted by the design institutes under the guidance of the Resettlement Office of
the project in collaboration with the relevant County Resettlement Offices (CROs) and
township governments and village leaders. The census survey of GMT and SMT was
conducted in February/March 1993 and updated in December 1995. The census survey
was carried out in April 1996 for the Connection Works while the survey for the Water
Treatment Plant and Booster Stations was conducted in June 1996.



-143 -                     ANNEX6
4.    All physical losses and the number of affected persons were inventoried on
household basis and signed by the family head and the village leaders. Relevant
information is recorded on the Household Registration Information Booklet, which will
be issued to all affected households.
Adverse Impacts
5.    Adverse impacts have been identified in the following categories: (a) acquisition
of 7,393 mu of agricultural land, (b) temporary leasing of 2,495 mu of agricultural land,
(c) relocation of 23 small enterprises, (d) resettlement of 54 persons in 16 households.
The impacts are detailed in Table 1.
6.    About 1,204 persons will lose land, including 54 persons in 16 households who
have lost both land and houses and have resettled in their new houses. 273 enterprise
employees will be affected due to the relocation of their enterprises. See Table 2.
Socioeconomic Surveys
7.    Socioeconomic surveys were conducted separately for GMT, SMT and the
Connection Works.  The surveys were undertaken by the Design Institutes in
collaboration with the local resettlement offices and governments in May 1996. The
surveys established the baseline living standards of the affected persons and provide the
basis for future comparisons.
C. LEGAL FRAMEWORK FOR LAND ACQUISITION AND RESETTLEMENT
8.    The Chinese government has issued a number of laws, regulations and guidelines
related to resettlement planning and implementation. Resettlement under the project is
prepared in accordance with these laws, regulations and guidelines. The main laws and
regulations concerning resettlement are listed in Table 3.
D. FRAMEWORK FOR PROJECT R&R IMPLEMENTATION
9.    The Project Resettlement Office has prepared separate land acquisition and
resettlement action plans (RAP) for the GMT, SMT, Connection Works and Huyan Water
Treatment Plant in accordance with the legal framework and the Bank OD 4.30. A
framework for R&R implementation has been laid out in the various RAPs.

Objectives and Principles of Land Acquisition and Resettlement
10.    The objective of the R&R is to ensure that the standards of living of all project-
affected persons are improved, or at least restored. To achieve the objective, the
following principles have been adhered to in the preparation of the RAPs:
(a)    Land acquisition and resettlement should be minimized as much as
possible
(b)    All structures should be paid at replacement cost without depreciation
(c)    Compensation should be paid to the owner collectives before  land
acquisition and used for productive purpose
(d)    All affected infrastructure would be replaced
(e)    Priority in job opportunities with the project should be given to project-
affected people
(f)    Land should be redistributed to farmers in all villages losing land to the
project
(g)    All affected enterprises would be assisted in relocation and workers would
be provided allowance during relocation
(h)    Full participation of the affected persons would be guaranteed during RAP
preparation and implementation
(i)    The affected persons should be able to redress their grievances

Compensation Policies For Different Categories of Project Adverse Impacts
11.    Land Acquisition.  Compensation for agricultural land permanently acquired is
estimated by applying specified multiplier to the average per mu annual output during the
past three years. Different compensation rates have been calculated for different types of
land in different areas, varying from Y 945 to Y 28,000 per mu. Details of compensation
calculation are provided in Table 4.
12.    Land Leasing. Compensation for land to be leased would be paid at three times
of their average per mu annual output, varying from Y 405 to Y 12,000 per mu. The
leasing period is normally two to three years, after which the project would return the
leased land fully restored in its previous productive condition. Any cost in restoring the
land productivity would be borne by the project.
13.    Structures.  Affected  structures would be compensated  at replacement cost,
which were estimated with market information in different areas and updated in early
1996. Details of the cost are provided in the RAPs.
14.    Impact on Enterprises. Affected enterprises would be provided alternative sites
free of cost. Affected buildings, structures, etc., would be paid at replacement costs
including relocation cost. Enterprise employees would be paid allowance equivalent to
monthly salaries during the period when production is stopped.

-148 -                             ANNEX6
16.    Impact on Infrastructure. All affected infrastructure would either be paid at full
replacement cost or reconstructed for the affected communities.
Resettlement of the Displaced Persons and Enterprises
17.    Resettlement. This project displaced 54 persons in 16 households along GMT.
New sites were identified and provided free of cost within the same village in 1993 and
compensation was paid fully to the PAPs by 1994. The farmers have built their new
houses with the compensation and salvageable materials from the demolished houses.
They have all resettled in the new houses.
18.    Relocation of Industrial Enterprises.  The project and complementary works
would affect 23 small enterprises, including 14 quarries, 1 brick factory, 7 coal-coking
factories and 1 reinforced-concrete prefabrication plant, affecting a total of 273 workers.
One coking plant and the reinforced concrete plant would only be partially affected and
would be paid full replacement cost for the affected structures and the rest need
relocation. New sites have been identified in consultation with the owners and will be
provided free of cost. The new sites are all nearby to maintain the same source of raw
materials. Replacement cost for reconstruction have been estimated by engineers from
the project and the enterprises. The project would pay full replacement cost for the
reconstruction of the plants, transportation cost to the new sites and profit loss during
production stoppage. See details in Table 5.

R&R Strategy of Rehabilitation
19.    The project will acquire a total of 7,393 mu of agricultural land, affecting 1,204
persons. The project, based on the findings of the field investigations and analysis of
local resources, has formulated the rehabilitation strategy through land development, off-
farm employment and pension arrangement.
20.    On-farm  Development. Given the rich land resources and poor cultivation in the
affected villages, land development is planned as the major rehabilitation measure.
YRDPC RO and design institutes, working closely with township and village
representatives, conducted field investigations to analyze land resources, the current
production levels and potentials of agriculture development in each village. Village-wise,
plans have been formulated for land development through slopeland and rotation land
terracing, wasteland reclamation and on-farm irrigation works. In villages where average
per capita land holding is above 5 mu, it is planned that 854 mu of dry flat land and
1,892 mu of dry slopeland will be distributed to the PAPs out of the remaining land. On-
farm works will be conducted to increase agricultural yield. In villages where per capita
landholding falls below 5 mu, it is planned to terrace 3,713 mu of slopeland and reclaim
148 mu of wasteland, which will be distributed to the affected persons to maintain per
capita landholding. A total of 983 PAPs will be provided agricultural land.
21.    Off-employment.  Some villages in the Connection Works Component have
planned to invest land compensation in off-farm developments and provide jobs to the
affected farmers in these enterprises. Some affected farmers have seen the opportunity in
transport business and have opted for self-employment with the compensation. 76 PAPs
will be engaged in either private or collective transport business. See details in Table 6.

-150 -                       ANNEX6
22.   Rehabilitation of Leased Land. The project will lease temporarily 2,495 mu of
agriculture land during construction, 1,489 mu of which is along the Connection Works.
The project will pay compensation for the leased land and return the land to the farmers
in its restored productive condition when leasing is over. The RAPs have included clear
rehabilitation standard of the leased land, the inspection and acceptance procedure and
rehabilitation schedule.
23.   Pension Arrangement. 126 elderly PAPs and children are eligible for pension in
Luyukou Village in the Connection Works Component. They will be provided Y 900 per
year per person for their pension. This pension will be provided to the old all their life
and to the children until they reach the age of 18.
24.   Support Services. YRDPC RO has drawn up detailed training program for the
affected farmers to equip them with new skills required for livelihood development
activities. PAP training will cover irrigated farming, vegetable growing, animal-rearing
and vehicle driving. The existing agricultural extension system will provide special
support to the affected villages in their livelihood development activities. They will
provide extension services to the PAPs, deliver timely agricultural input including seeds,
fertilizer, pesticide and agricultural machinery services. County governments will be
responsible for the construction of all necessary irrigation facilities.
Preferential Policy
25.   Shanxi Provincial Government has issued "Preferential Policy for Resettlement
And Rehabilitation of the Affected Persons in Wanjiazhai Water Transfer Project."
Major provisions are as follows:
(a)   Any houses, public buildings, enterprise and public facilities to be
constructed under the R&R program will be exempted from charges for
urban infrastructure construction, tax for farmland occupation.
(b)   Enterprises for resettlement, collective or private, would be exempted
from income tax for three years from the time of yielding profit.
(c)    Orchard developed for PAPs would be exempted from forest and orchard
tax for 1-3 years.
(d)   Newly developed land would be exempted from agriculture tax for three to
five years.
(e)   Priority in employment would be given to PAPs in the construction site
and the benefited areas.
(f)    Special care should be given to PAP children in school education in the
affected areas



-151-                      ANNEX6
(g)   Priority should be given to PAPs in providing agriculture credit and low-
interest loans.
(h)   An reservoir construction fund is planned to be created with project profits
to help livelihood development of the PAPs.
Implementation Schedule
26.   RAP implementation schedule is dovetailed with the construction plan of the civil
works. Land acquisition and resettlement for the GMT had been completed by April
1996 while livelihood development activities are still underway and will be completed in
1997. Land acquisition on SMT, started already, will continue till the end of 1998 and
livelihood development activities will continue till 2001. RAP implementation will start
in 1997 for the Connection Works and will be completed in 2001. RAP implementation
for the Water Treatment Plant started in 1996 and will be completed in 1997. YRDPC
RO has prepared a detailed CPM schedule of all land acquisition and livelihood
development activities for all components of the project. This CPM schedule will be
used to monitor the progress of R&R activities and will be updated semiannually.
Institutional Framework
27.   A complete R&R institutional framework has been set up for the implementation
of land acquisition and resettlement under the project.
28.   Project Bureau (YRDPC). It is responsible for overall R&R implementation on
behalf of Shanxi Provincial Government.
29.   Project Resettlement Office (YRDPCRO). YRDPC RO has been established
within YRDPC with four full-time staff, experienced in resettlement. It has the overall
responsibility for the planning, coordination, supervising of land acquisition and R&R
activities and R&R staff training under the project.
30.   Field Resettlement Offices. Resettlement offices have been established in the
three field construction offices, each with three to five staff. They are responsible for
land acquisition, contracting with local governments, supervising R&R progress. They
will provide necessary support to CROs and TROs in RAP implementation. They will
report to YRDPC RO.
31.   County Resettlement Office (CRO). CROs have been set up in each of the
affected counties, each staffed with 5 to 10 persons. They are responsible for the
planning and implementation of livelihood developments, payment of compensation to
affected villages and coordination of land acquisition, resettlement and civil works. They
will submit quarterly R&R progress reports to the field offices.
32.   Township Resettlement Office (TRO). TROs have been set up in the township
governments. They are mainly responsible for disseminating resettlement policies to



-152 -                      ANNEX6
affected villages, supervising and assisting villages in land development and land
redistribution.
Participation And Consultation
33.   Project R&R planning has been undertaken in a participatory manner.  All
relevant line agencies, administrations, entities and communities were consulted
systematically in R&R planning. Particular attention was devoted to the participation of
and consultation with the affected communities.
34.   Project information was disseminated to the PAPs at an early stage. Information
dissemination meetings were held at the village level, where project information, possible
adverse impacts, suggested compensation rates, resettlement arrangements, proposals for
rehabilitation were presented and discussed with the PAPs. The RAPs were revised with
suggestions from the PAPs. A resettlement information booklet was prepared. After the
review of the RAP by the Bank, the RIB will be reproduced and distributed to all the
PAPs' households.
35.   Village leaders and representatives of the villagers participated actively in the
census and socioeconomic survey carried out by YRDPC RO, CROs and design
institutes. The results of the census were recorded and signed by village leaders. The
villagers have also contributed to RAP preparation, particularly in the formulation of
livelihood development programs.
36.   Consultation with the affected communities is planned to continue until the
project is completed. Field surveys and meetings have been held with affected villagers
to evaluate the completed R&R programs along the GMT, SMT and propose additional
measures. YRDPC RO plans (a) to undertake bimonthly regular surveys of the affected
persons over R&R implementation, covering, at least, 40 percent of total affected persons
and (b) to hold public meetings with affected persons once a month to improve R&R
implementation.
Grievance Mechanism
37.   Shanxi Government has grievance redress offices at various levels. They have
been notified to give special attention to redress of grievances from PAPs regarding any
aspects of land acquisition and resettlement under the project. PAPs can approach these
offices to seek redress of their grievances. PAPs also have the right to appeal to the court
to seek resolution of their grievances.
38.   Apart from the existing grievance redress mechanisms, Shanxi Government has
established a three-stage grievance channel for project PAPs:
(a)   If any affected person is aggrieved by any aspect of the resettlement and
rehabilitation program, he/she can lodge an oral or written grievance with
the TROs through the village committees. In case an oral complaint is



-153 -                     ANNEX6
made, it will be written on paper by the village unit and processed.
Village Administration Committee or the TRO will resolve the issue
within two weeks.
(b)   If the aggrieved person is not satisfied with the decision reached in Stage
1, he/she can bring the complaint to the attention of the CRO within one
month from the date of the receipt of the decision taken in Stage 1. CRO
will reach a decision on the complaint within two weeks.
(c)   If the aggrieved person is not satisfied with the decision of the CRO,
he/she can bring the complaint to the attention of the YRDPC RO within
one month from the date of the receipt of the decision in Stage 2. YRDPC
RO will reach a decision on the complaint within three weeks.
39.   Detailed procedures for redress of grievance and of the appeal process will be
publicized through posting in the affected villages and their adequacy will be monitored
throughout RAP implementation. All grievances will be recorded in standard formats.
Monitoring and Evaluation
40.   Monitoring includes both internal and external monitoring. The primary target is
to (a) evaluate the progress of R&R programs implementation, and (b) modify and
improve R&R plans as necessary during implementation and evaluate the result of R&R
programs.
41.   Internal Monitoring. Internal monitoring of the R&R programs is part of the
overall project management. YRDPC RO will be responsible for internal monitoring,
that will be conducted through the R&R institutional setup. The monitoring indicators
would include, at least, institutional capacity, R&R staff training, land acquisition, land
leasing, payment of compensation, land development and redistribution, off-farm
development activities, PAP training, restoration of public facilities, relocation of
enterprises. Monitoring reports would be submitted quarterly and semiannual monitoring
reports will be submitted to the Bank as part of the overall project progress report.
Detailed reporting formats have been developed and are attached to the RAPs.
42.   External Monitoring. YRDPC plans to have the Resettlement Office of Yellow
River Water Conservancy Committee (YRCCRO) as its independent external monitor for
the project. YRCCRO will set up a monitoring team for the project, staffed with 15
resettlement specialists including 5 senior staff. External monitoring would focus on
(a) the physical progress of RAP implementation, (b) evaluation of livelihood restoration
and living standard improvement, (c) PAP participation and consultation during
implementation, (d) effectiveness of grievances redress mechanism and (e) proposing
measures for improvement.
43.   External monitoring will be conducted through regular consultation meetings with
the affected communities, regular field visits, structured and random sampling of the



-154 -                                ANNEX6
affected persons on living standard. Living standard will be monitored on a sample basis.
A data base will be maintained and updated twice a year with first hand data. Two living
standard surveys will be conducted among the affected population, one after two years of
resettlement completion and one at the completion of the project. YRCCRO will submit
its semiannual monitoring reports to YRDPCRO and the Bank throughout the project
implementation  period.   Detailed  monitoring  indicators, survey  questionnaires  and
reporting formats have been developed and attached to the RAPs.
44.    Environmental and Resettlement Advisory Panel. The project has established
a seven-member international Environment And Resettlement Advisory Panel. The panel
will meet twice a year to review R&R progress, propose measures for improvements.
The panel will submit its report to both the project management and the Bank.

is allocated across project components as follows: Y 7.33 million for GMT, Y 12.41
million for SMT and Y 20.35 million for Connection Works. Price contingency is
estimated at 7 percent and is included in the annual costs. Shanxi Province Government
will finance all costs for land acquisition and resettlement. The cost breakdown and

46.   All compensation will be paid before acquisition and a disbursement procedure

compensation for productive purpose and pay the PAPs for their private assets lost.
E. EVALUATION OF COMPLETED R&R UNDER THE PROJECT
Land Acquisition And Resettlement
47.   Land acquisition for the GMT has been completed. Land acquired included
1,129 mu of cultivated land, 67 mu of riverbank land, 420 mu of rotation land, 7 mu of
orchards, 99 mu of forest land and 69 mu of bush land. A total of 714 mu of land were
leased. A total amount of Y 6.87 million have been paid for compensation. Some
114 mu of land have been acquired in seven villages for the SMT and the total amount of
compensation paid is Y 0.28 million.
48.   The resettlement of the 16 households is completed. The PAPs are resettled
within the same village. Their new houses are larger in area and of better quality.
Livelihood Development Activities
49.   Land development has been going on. So far 1,560 mu of land have been
redistributed in the affected villages including the newly developed and terraced land.
Land development will be completed in October 2001.
50.   The project improved the infrastructure in the villages along the transmission line.
Three highways have been constructed in Pianguan County with a total length of 127 km
and one road has been rehabilitated with a length of 25 km. As a result, 23 villages have
become accessible through the new highways. The project has drilled 12 deep wells
along the GMT and has provided 3,000 people and 750 large animals in 10 villages along
the line with drinking and irrigation water. The project helped with the power supply for
over 400 households by building over 6 km of transmission lines.
Living Standard Survey
51.  In April 1996, Tianjin Water Resources and Hydroelectric Design Institute of
MWR conducted a survey to evaluate living standard improvement among PAPs along
the GMT and the SMT and local economic development with the project. The survey is
undertaken by random sampling 26 percent of PAP households and collecting data
through secondary sources. The survey indicates a remarkable improvement in living
standards of the PAPs and fast economic development in Pianguan County with the
project:
(a)   Diversified sources of income. The number of households with no other
source of income than farming dropped from 82 percent in 1992 to 12



-156 -                      ANNEX6
percent. Most of the families have either opened family business, sideline
activities or have members working as temporary laborers.
(b)   Increase of average per capita income from Y 100 to Y 833 in 1992 to
Y 625 to Y 5,000 in 1995. While 59 percent of the households had an
average annual per capita income of below Y 500 in 1992, 1995 witnessed
59 percent of them enjoying an average per capita income of over Y 3,000.
(c)   An impressive possession of modem electronic apparatus and vehicles
such as color TVs, small tractors, refrigerators, stereo systems, motor
bikes and washing machines, rare before the project started.
(d)   Improved housing conditions with better quality and larger area.
(e)   Access to clean drinking water.
(f)   The 152 km of highway have created a transport network within Pianguan
County connecting 15 townships and have greatly improved transportation
for the affected villages.
(g)   With the project, the number of construction companies in the county
jumped from 67 before the project to 189 in 1996 with the total revenue
increased by 400 percent. Private transport businesses increased from 58
in 1992 to 1406 in 1996 while the number of restaurants went up by 300
percent.
(h)   Since the project started construction, new  enterprises have been
established, including 2 cement plants, 35 quarries, 21 kilns, 46 brick
factories and 50 new shops along project transmission lines with about
4,500 employees.
F. WANJIAZHAI DAM AND RESERVOIR PROJECT
Introduction
52.   Wanjiazhai Multipurpose Dam and Reservoir Project (WJZP) is a local project
financed by the Ministry of Water Resources, Shanxi Province and Nei Mongol Region.
It is located on the Yellow River, which separates Shanxi Province and Nei Mongol
Region. The reservoir would provide 1.4 billion m3 annually to the area. Shanxi
Province plans to channel its share of water through the project, to be financed by the
Bank.
53.   The reservoir damsite construction affected three villages. Its resettlement started
in 1993 and was completed in 1996. Reservoir inundation would affect 60 villages in
two counties and one banner and 90 percent of the affected population are in Qinshuihe
County in Nei Mongol Region.



-157 -                                   ANNEX6
Resettlement Planning
54.      Inventory and Socioeconomic Surveys.  Resettlement planning started in 1989.
The census survey was conducted in February 1990, updated in 1993 and 1996. The
census was carried out by the Regional, county, township resettlement offices and design
institutes. Villagers participated actively in the surveys.
55.      Resettlement Impacts. The project will submerge 60 villages in 10 townships in
three counties, inundating 5,171 mu of farmland. A total population of 6,047 will have to
be resettled including 4,645 PAPs losing houses and 1,402 persons only losing land. The
main categories of losses and the number of affected population is detailed in Table 8.
56.      Resettlement Objectives.   Resettlement action  plans were  prepared  for each
county by county resettlement offices. The overall objective of resettlement is the
restoration and improvement of the current living standards of the resettlers and will be
materialize through four specific targets of (a) economic development in reaching, at
least, the same level of the hosting population in average per capita output value, income
and grain consumption; (b) social development with an enhanced level of education,
technology, improved health services, better health and rehabilitated and improved
infrastructure in transportation, telecommunication and power; (c) environment
development in expanded forest coverage, reduced earth erosion and better treatment of
gas and water pollution in the resettlement areas.
