- 252 -                    ANNEX 17
12.   If an extremely large flood occurs and the pool level goes up to 1,130m,
emergency measures should be started according to order issued by Provincial Flood
Protection Headquarters (PFPH). The emergency task forces, including the army, public
utilities and farmers, will promptly arrive to the damsite to heighten urgently the dam by
constructing a small dike to the elevation 1, 1 34.3m. At the same time, the PFPH will call
for immediate evacuation of the downstream affected area.
13.  In case the pool level ups to 1,131m, the saddle dam on right bank would be
artificially broken, if necessary. The maximum discharge due to this artificial breaking
would be 83,500 m3/second. According to the result of flood routing, the maximum
discharge at Yingze Bridge, Taiyuan City would be 40,000 m3/second, much greater than
the allowable 3,450 m3/second.
14.   The Emergency Preparedness Plan has been preliminarily considered in the
Operation Plan for Flood Protection. But it seems not complete enough. It is suggested
that more detailed Emergency Preparedness Plan be proceeded, taking into account the
Guidelines for Emergency Preparedness Plan, provided as Attachment 3.
15.   Wanjiazhai Dam. The Wanjiazhai Dam is located on the main stem of the
Yellow River in the middle reach, 30 km northwest of Pianguan County, Shanxi
Province. The dam is of concrete gravity type, 105m high, with the total storage and
regulating capacity of 896 and 445 million m3 respectively. The two intakes for the
YRDP are set up in the dam near the left abutment.
16.   The dam is not under the Yellow River Diversion Project, but is being constructed
by MWR. By the end of 1995, 256,000 m3 of concrete have been placed in the dam body.
According to the schedule, 500,000 m3 of concrete will be placed in 1996. It is planned
that the dam will be completed by the end of 1998.
17.   Detailed description of the dam was given in "Current Status of Design and
Construction of Wanjiazhai Water Project on Yellow River" prepared by Messrs. Zhang
Zezhen and Chen Yiming on September 30, 1995. The Dam Safety Inspection, Operation
and Maintenance Plan and Emergency Preparedness Plan are discussed below.
18.   Dam Safety Inspection. The design of the dam is prepared by TIDI. It has been
reviewed by China International Engineering Consultative Corporation in 1990 and by
General Planning and Design Institute, MWR in 1993 and 1995. A special team of
experts has visited the damsite providing consultancy on the design in October 1991. Up
to now, no permanent Panel of Experts has been set up.
19.   Through Local Competitive Bidding, the contracts of the dam and the hydropower
plant were awarded to the 4th and 6th Construction Bureaus of Hydro and Hydropower
respectively. The Northeast Hydro and Hydropower Investigation and Design Institute
undertakes the construction supervision, acting as Engineer.



- 253 -                     ANNEX 17
20.   Taking into account the importance of the dam project and also based on the
operational policies of the World Bank, it is recommended that the Dam Safety
Inspection Panel will be organized by MWR to undertake periodic, comprehensive and
independent review to evaluate features and actions pertaining to the safety of the dam
and appurtenant structures during the course of construction and operation. For the
purpose of satisfactory implementation, the Terms of Reference for Wanjiazhai Dam
Safety Inspection Panel is provided as Attachment 2.
21.   Operation and Maintenance Plan. Due to the high silt content of Yellow River
during flood season, the basic criterion of the operation program of the reservoir involves
impounding the clear water and discharging the muddy water. Each year in August and
September, the pool level will usually be lowered to 952-957 m for flushing the sediment.
From mid July to mid October, the pool level should not be higher than 966 m for
maintaining the storage capacity of flood regulation.   The highest pool level
corresponding to 1: 10,000 years flood would be 979.1 m.
22.   The impoundment of the reservoir will be started in mid-October.  From
November to February of next year, the pool level shall be maintained at 975 m or lower
for ice control, because this is the period of ice flowing before freezing-up. From the
beginning of March to the beginning of April, the pool level shall be lowered to 970 m
for melting ice control. After that time, the pool level can be raised to 980 m.
23.   The above mentioned operation program  is stipulated in principle in the
preliminary design. The maintenance program has not been prepared yet. It is suggested
that the Operation and Maintenance Plan should be prepared before initial reservoir
filling, generally in conformity with the guidelines given in Attachment 4.
24.   Emergency Preparedness Plan. According to the preliminary design, the results
of flood regulation are as follows:

25.   During discussion, TIDI considered that there are following favorable conditions
preventing the failure of the dam:



- 254 -                    ANNEX 17
(a)   The dam is built on sound and thick limestone foundation without
developed geotechnical structures, and is located in the region of low
seismic intensity (six degree).
(b)   The results of flood regulation did not include the service of the surface
spillway, which will be operated as extraordinary measure with additional
discharge capacity of 864 m3/second.
(c)   In case of emergency, the pool level can be drawn down from 977m to
915m in five days with the help of large discharge capacity of medium and
bottom outlet works.
(d)   The crest elevation of the concrete gravity dam is 982m, with the
freeboard of 2.9m above highest flood pool level. Even the extremely big
flood should occur, the sustainability of the gravity dam against
overtopping would be considerable.
26.   TIDI has examined the effects of a check flood of 1 in 10,000 years, however,
they have not examined the effect of the PMF type flood and dam failure caused by
nuclear attack.
27.   As for the instrumentation and monitoring system, flood forecasting and
communication system, and other facilities which are closely related to safety of regular
operation and in case of emergency, have been designed.
28.   Downstream of the dam, the existing Tianqiao hydropower station is located 110
km from Wanjiazhai, and also some villages, townships exist on small flood plains in
Yellow River tributaries. The Tianqiao hydropower station is composed of 190m long
concrete gravity dam on the left bank and 330m long earthfill dam on the right bank. The
heights of the concrete and earthfill dams are 42 and 23m respectively. While the storage
capacity of the reservoir is 66 million m3, and the installed generating capacity is 128
MW. The maximum discharge capacity of spillway is 17,010 m3/second corresponding to
the probability of 0.2 percent
29.   The Owner of the Wanjiazhai dam project is Wanjiazhai Dam Construction
Management Bureau (WDCMB), under MWR. At present, the Emergency Preparedness
Plan has not been formulated yet. Considering the importance of the dam and the
catastrophic consequence of the dam incident, assurance have been obtained during
negotiations that an Emergency Preparedness Plan would be formulated by WDCMB
taking into account the Guide Lines for Emergency Preparedness Plan (Attachment 3) by
December 31, 1998.

ATTACHMENT 1: TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR FEN-1 DAM SAFETY INSPECTION PANEL
General
1.    A Panel of Experts will be appointed by Department of Water Resources of
Shanxi Province (DWRSP) to undertake periodic, comprehensive and independent review
to evaluate features and actions pertaining to the safety of the dam and appurtenant
structures. The Panel is guided by the dam safety assurance objectives of the authority
and by related legislation, regulations, standards and criteria.
Organization and Membership
2.    The Panel shall contain seven members with wide, specialized experience in the
following fields:
* Flood Hydrology
* Geotechnique
* Earth Dam and Appurtenan-t Hydraulic Structure Design
* Sedimentology
* Instrumentation
* Construction
* Mechanical and Electrical Design
3.    A Chairman will be appointed by DWRSP to coordinate communications, to call
and chair its meetings, to ensure the membership's activity and to integrate the reviews
and recommendations. The Chairman should have a broad technical understanding of
dam engineering and experience in serving on a similar panel for a dam of comparable
magnitude, complexity, and characteristics.
Meetings and Schedule
4.    The Panel will convene once every five years to inspect dam safety. It is
recommended that the first meeting be held before September 1998.
5.    The Panel will prepare and submit written proceedings of the meetings, including
recommendations, within three weeks of the meetings, and in case of emergency will
prepare technical memoranda or aide memories during the meetings. A preliminary
report will be prepared before the adjournment of each meeting. All reports will be
submitted to DWRSP and YRDPC, and through the latter to the World Bank. It is
expected that the first report will be submitted to the World Bank by December 31, 1998.
Scope of Reviews
6.    The subjects on which the Panel are expected to comment are listed below. The
Panel should also comment on any other matter which it perceives to be important to the
dam safety.



- 256 -                     ANNEX 17
(a)   Assessment on hydrological analysis results taking into account the new
hydrometeorological data and changed runoff conditions.
(b)   Adequacy of siltation monitoring program.
(c)   Effectiveness of instrumentation system, including the efficiency of
different instruments, data collecting and processing system.
(d)   Evaluation of performance behavior of the dam and appurtenant structures.
(e)   Efficiency of flood forecasting and warning system.
(f)    Appropriateness of Operation and Maintenance Plan.
(g)   Availability and workability of Emergency Preparedness Plan.



- 257 -                    ANNEX 17
ATTACHMENT 2: TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR WANJIAZHAI DAM SAFETY INSPECTION
PANEL
General
1.    The Panel of Experts will be appointed by MWR, to undertake periodic,
comprehensive and independent review to evaluate features and actions pertaining to the
safety of the dam and appurtenant structures. The Panel is guided by the dam safety
assurance objectives of the cognizant authority and by related legislations, regulations,
standards and criteria.
Organization and Membership
2.    The Panel shall contain four permanent members with wide, specialized
experience in the following fields:
* Engineering Geology
 Hydraulic Design
* Planning and Design of Darn and Hydropower Facilities
* Construction of Concrete Dam, and Hydropower Facilities
3.    At appropriate times, the Panel will be enlarged as necessary by the addition of
specialists in other fields, such as hydrology, sedimentology, hydraulic turbines and in
any other area, where the Chairman of the Panel, in consultation with MWR, considers it
advisable.
4.    A Chairman will be appointed by MWR to coordinate communications, to call
and chair its meetings, to ensure the membership's activity and to provide balance to its
reviews and recommendations.
5.    The composition of the Panel, and the areas of expertise which it covers may be
varied during the course of construction and operation of the Dam as considered
appropriate by MWR in consultation with the Chairman.
Meetings and Schedules
6.    The Panel will convene at regular intervals to review the status of work in
progress. The frequency of meetings and their timing will be adjusted to conform with
the schedule of works in progress, but the time between meetings shall not normally
exceed twelve months during construction and initial period of operation. At each
meeting the scheduled dates for the next meeting and tentative timing for the subsequent
meeting will normally be fixed, to enable Panel members to arrange their individual
schedules.
7.    The Panel will prepare and submit written proceedings of the meetings, including
recommendations, within three weeks of the meetings, and in case of emergency will



- 258 -                      ANNEX 17
prepare technical memoranda or aide memoirs during the meetings. A preliminary report
will be prepared before the adjournment of each meeting. All reports will be submitted to
MWR and YRDPC and through the latter to the World Bank.
Scope of Reviews
8.    The subjects on which the Panel is expected to comment are listed below. The
Panel should also comment on any other matter which it perceives to be important to the
successful completion and operation of the project.
(a)    Assessment on hydrometeorological data and changed runoff conditions.
(b)   The sufficiency of the geological investigations and the interpretation
thereof, the engineering implications with respect to foundation design,
stability of natural and excavated slopes at dam site and reservoir area.
(c)    Estimates of siltation progress and efficacy of sediment flushing facilities.
(d)   Adequacy of the design of concrete dam, hydraulic structures and
hydropower facilities.
(e)   Appropriateness of construction planning, quality assurance procedures
and construction supervision.
(f)    Adequacy of siltation monitoring program.
(g)   Effectiveness of instrumentation system, including the efficiency of
different instruments, data collecting and processing system.
(h)    Suitability of the plan for initial reservoir filling .
(i)    Efficiency of flood forecasting and warning system.
G)    Appropriateness of Operation and Maintenance Plan.
(k)   Availability and workability of Emergency Preparedness Plan.



- 259 -                     ANNEX 17
ATTACHMENT 3: GUIDELINES FOR EMERGENCY PREPAREDNESS PLAN
1.    A detailed Emergency Preparedness Plan (EPP) should be established for each
dam within the drainage area or operating system as a whole. If there is more than one
system operating within the same drainage area, the EPP should be coordinated by a joint
committee on emergency operation composed of representatives of all operating
organizations. The EPP should be approved by the Goveniment Agency.
2.    EPP should be reviewed at regular intervals for the need of updating and
adaptation to alterations of the physical and social environment, if necessary.
Appropriate intervals for the review may be periods of five to ten years depending upon
the progress of regional development.
3.    EPP should deal with, but not be limited to, the following aspects:
* hydrographic observation and flood warning scheme;
. drawdown and flood control operation of reservoir;
. emergency emptying of the reservoir;
. inundation maps for flows up to the design flood, and for catastrophic
conditions caused by dam failure;
* evacuation of flood-threatened areas;
. rescue operations and other emergency provisions;
. equipment, material and support available for emergency relief;
. coordination of emergency relief actions with third parties (for instance: civil
defense, police, hospitals, etc.);
. emergency standby of public utilities;
. emergency operation of power plant, water supply scheme associated with the
dam;
* emergency warning;
* emergency communication;
* emergency transportation;
. emergency access to the damsite;
* emergency decision-making process and procedures.
4.    EPP may be done for several types and modes of emergency but should include
the analysis of the most severe possibility; that is, the instantaneous failure of the dam.
The possible effect of the failure of upstream dams should also be taken into account.
5.    EPP should cope with emergency precautions and possible emergency repair
measures at the dam site and with warning and emergency relief action downstream of
the dam.
6.    Flood warning and emergency warning systems should be checked for reliability
and efficiency before the beginning of each flood season.



- 260 -                    ANNEX 17
7.    EPP should include instructions to be followed by the local operating staff in the
event of loss of communications with the leading control agency.
8.   In case of imminent danger or of a major accident, corrective action must be taken
immediately and independently of normal administrative procedures. Enough authority
should be vested in the operator's top level technical personnel to order emergency
preventive or repair measures without asking for special authorization from management.
9.    Clear and easily understandable emergency instructions should be issued to all
operating units. These emergency instructions, which must include a definition of the
supervising units authorized or obliged to issue orders under emergency conditions,
should be easily accessible. The need for updating should be checked periodically and
always after institutional, operational and administrative changes.
10.   Operating staff should be trained and periodically retrained in emergency
operations.



- 261-                      ANNEX 17
ATTACHMENT 4: GUIDELINES FOR DAM OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE
1.    The operation of a dam and reservoir needs to be understood in the context of the
multiple user who are involved, contractual agreements therewith, and best efforts
possible to optimize benefits for all.
2.    For each dam and reservoir, a reservoir capacity allocation scheme should be
prepared. The scheme should usually include the following items:
* Reservoir capacity allocation for different uses at several elevations and a
reference to the use allocations made in planning and designing the project.
. Flood regulation criteria and flood discharges.
* Sediment regulating rules and siltation.
* Water supply for irrigation.
. Water supply for municipal and industrial uses.
* Hydropower generating operation.
3.    To ensure the operational safety, the performance of the dam and appurtenant
structures should be carefully monitored. The monitoring should include, but not be
limited to, the following items:
4.    Instrumentation system, including the surface and embedded devices, should be
monitored at regular intervals. The accuracy of data obtained from the readings should be
checked annually for two or three years after commissioning of the dam and later at
longer intervals. The actual loads and loading combinations acting upon the structure
should be compared with those of the original design. At the same time, the original
design criteria and safety strategy should be reviewed with emphasis on the compatibility
with current technology.
5.    Visual examination of structures should be carried out at regular intervals. The
exposed surfaces of a concrete dam and appurtenant concrete structures should be
visually examined for cracks, spelling, leaching, leakage, indication of deterioration or
chemical reactions and damage from erosion or cavitation, etc.
6.    Earth rock fill embankments should be examined for cracks, leakage, saturated
areas, springs, sinkholes, evidence of piping, erosion, frost heave, crest alignment,
bulging or depression of slopes and berms, animal burrows, and the deterioration of
riprap or other slope protection materials.
7.    If the visual examination reveals evidence of material deterioration or unsafe
structural behavior, or yields doubts about the structural and/or operational safety, a more
in-depth investigation by core drilling, excavation of observation pits and/or other
appropriate methods should be initiated immediately.
8.    Underwater examinatioi should be made periodically for those parts which are
permanently submerged, such as lower part of the upstream slope or face of a dam and



- 262 -                     ANNEX 17
stilling basins. The examination can be implemented by sounding and/or by underwater
television camera.
9.    Drainage systems and uplift pressure relief devices should be examined for
possible obstruction, deterioration or damage by chemical reactions or bacterial growth.
Sources of seepage should be pinpointed and flow rate and quality (clear or muddy water)
should be investigated for comparison with previous observations and the results of
permeability computations.  Any anomalous changes in seepage volume shall be
investigated immediately.
10.   All mechanical and associated electrical equipment of the dam  should be
examined for proper functioning and adequate maintenance. Besides the accuracy of
operating performance, inspection should extend to lubrication and the functional
integrity of the equipment. Corroded, damaged or worn parts shall be replaced. An
adequate stock of spare parts must be maintained throughout the dam's service life.
11.   The service and emergency power sources and transmission should be examined
with special attention to the power supply under region-wide natural catastrophic
conditions.
12.   Siltation of the reservoir should be annually monitored by sounding.
13.   Critical areas of the reservoir rim should be inspected annually for five years and
later at least every three years for landslides and the indication of the development of
problems that might affect the safety of the dam or reservoir.
14.   The whole reservoir and its surroundings should remain under permanent
surveillance with respect to possible health problems. If foci of waterborne or water-
related diseases should develop, they must be brought under specialized medical control
immediately.
15.   Though pollution is normally not a direct consequence of reservoir or dam
operation, the operation unit should make every possible effort to detect sources of
pollution in order to enable the public health and other government authorities to enforce
pollution control.
16.   The adequacy and proper functioning of monitoring instruments and devices
should be checked at least every two years. The accuracy and correct functioning of the
hydrographic observation system, inclusive of telemetering and transmission devices,
should be checked before the beginning of every flood season.
17.   The sequence and frequency of the reading of monitoring instruments and
observation devices should follow the specific instructions given by the designer during
initial stage of operation, and later on can be revised according to the variation tendency
derived from accumulated data of previous years for different instruments and devices.



- 263 -                     ANNEX 17
18.   The readings of monitoring system should be processed and interpreted without
delay. Data and information should be carefully identified and filed for appraisal and
reference during the periodic inspections. Any substantial deviation from previous
observations or the anticipated behavior of the structure shall be brought immediately to
the attention of the inspection team.
19.   An inspection schedule should be established jointly by the operator and the
inspection team. This schedule should be set utp in accordance with the convenience and
requirements of operation. It would be advantageous to schedule the principal inspection
activities to coincide with major maintenance operations to facilitate the inspection of
equipment and the dewatering of water conduits, pump pits etc..
20.   A description of the methods and procedures employed for inspection and the
findings and resulting recommendations should be summarized in the inspection report.
Detected irregularities should be mapped for future reference and comparison. If any
remedial actions are deemed necessary, they should be proposed by clear
recommendations.  The report should be prepared immediately after finishing the
inspection and issued without delay.
